Organization Decisioncriteria.Surveyresults.Thedecision-makingprocessconsidersseveralcriteria and that aid inreaching a decision.Currently, inOman, cost-effectiveness andbudget impact Management analysiswerethemostcommoncriteriareportedtobeconsideredinthepolicyprocessby 38%(n58)and33%(n57)ofrespondents,respectively. 251 In the future, respondents preferred considering more criteria in the decision-making processincludingunmetmedicalneed(52%,n511),healthcarepriority(57%,n512), therapeutic value (71%, n 5 15), on top of cost-effectiveness (81%, n 5 17), and budget impact(81%,n517).Respondentsindicatedthatcurrentlyexplicitmulti-criteriadecision analysis(MCDA)frameworkisnotapplied.However,inthefuture95%(n520)wouldprefer applyingMCDAtojudgethevalueofselectedhealthtechnologiesbasedonmultiplecriteria. Forthecost-effectivenessthreshold,mostsurveyrespondents(81%,n517)indicatedthe absence of a cost-effectiveness threshold in Oman. In the future, 95% (n 5 20) of survey respondents would prefer adopting cost-effectiveness thresholds, of which 81% (n 5 17) preferredexplicitthresholdsoverimplicitones.Outofthe81%(n517)preferringexplicit thresholds,57%(n512)wouldliketoadoptexplicitsoftthresholds. Explicit hard thresholds rely only on the cost-effectiveness of a health technology for resource allocation decisions, while explicit soft thresholds are more flexible allowing negotiationsandothercriteriatobeconsideredotherthancost-effectiveness(Eichleretal., 2004). In other words, if the incremental cost-effectiveness ratio (ICER) of a technology exceeds the hard threshold value, negotiation is not permitted, and the technology is not reimbursed. However, with soft thresholds, there is a chance for the reimbursement of technologiesthatarenotcost-effectiveafterpricenegotiationortakingintoaccountother criteria(Eichleretal.,2004). Validationresults(roundtablediscussion).Expertswerealignedontheuseofexplicitsoft thresholdsandMCDA.AsGDPpercapitaisthemostfrequentlyappliedreferencepointfor establishingcost-effectivenessthresholds(Griffithsetal.,2015),theyrecommendedtheuse ofmultiplethresholdsbasedon1-3timestheGDPpercapitaasastartingpointinthefirst 2years.Duringthisperiod,effortswillbemadetoestablishacost-effectivenessthreshold specifictoOmanbythethirdyear(3-5years).RegardingMCDA,itwasrecommendedto implementMCDAforselecteddecisionproblemsasapilotinthefirst2yearsandexpandits usein3-5years. QualityandtransparencyofHTAimplementation.Surveyresults.Toimprovethequality ofHTA,severalapproachesareavailable,includingpublishingmethodologicalguidelines fortheassessmentprocess,publishingappraisalreportstogetherwithacriticalappraisal checklistandfollowinguponpreviousrecommendations.InOman,the greatmajorityof respondents(86%,n518)reportedthatnoneofthequalityelementsareutilizedtoimprove HTA quality. In the future, they preferred having a publicly available critical appraisal checklist(76%,n516),publishedmethodologicalguidelines(52%,n511)andfollowingup onHTArecommendations(33%,n57). Technologyassessment,criticalappraisalreports,andHTArecommendationsarecurrently not accessible to the public as reported by 95% (n5 20) of the respondents. However, 90% (n519)ofrespondentspreferredthemtobepublishedinthefuture.Whenitcametothetimelines ofHTAsubmissionsandissuingrecommendations,95%(n519)oftherespondentsreportedthe absenceoftransparenttimelines.However,inthefuture86%(n518)ofrespondentspreferred havingtransparenttimelinesforHTAsubmissionsaswellasissuingrecommendations. Validationresults(roundtablediscussion).Expertsrecommendedpilottestingduringthe first year of HTA implementation. Pilot testing, involving testing the HTA under real conditionsandcollectingfeedback,willallowexpertstodecideoncleartimelinesstarting
JHOM from the second year. As for transparency, experts recommended to start by publishing 38,9 recommendationsoftheappraisalprocessduringthefirst5yearsfollowedbypublishingfull appraisalreportsfrom6-10years. Localdata.Surveyresults.LocaldatawasnotrequiredinthecurrentHTAprocessasreported by74%(n514)ofsurveyrespondents.Inthefuture,mostsurveyrespondents(81%,n517) preferred mandating the use of local data for HTA evidence together with assessing the transferabilityofinternationaldataintheabsenceoflocaldata.Morethan70%(n515)ofsurvey 252 respondentsreportedlimitedavailabilityoraccessibilitytolocalreal-worlddata.Inthefuture, 95%(n520)ofrespondentspreferredallocatingmoreresourcestoestablishingpatientregistries incertaindiseaseareasandallowingpayer'sdatabasestobeaccessibleforHTAdoers. Validation results (round table discussion). For the short term, experts recommended usingthecurrentlyavailablelocaldatainadditiontobuildingadatawarehousetosupport HTA which can be ready to use from 3-5 years. Furthermore, the currently available electronic claims database in Oman can serve as a source for local cost and resource utilization data after some modification in its structure limiting the dependence on internationaldataandassessingtheirtransferability. Internationalcollaboration.Surveyresults.Allsurveyrespondentsreportedthatcurrently they are not involved in any joint international work. In the future, 90% (n 5 18) of respondents preferred the adaptation of HTA materials developed by international HTA bodies. Currently, all respondents indicated limited participation in international courses relatedtoHTAwhileinthefuture,86%(n518)ofrespondentspreferredparticipatingor evendevelopinginternationalHTAcourses. Validationresults(roundtablediscussion).Expertsrecommendedcollaborationthrough theGulfCooperationCouncil(GCC)andtheGulfHealthCouncil.Omancanthereforebenefit fromexchangingexperiencesandreusingHTAmaterialsdevelopedbyotherGCCcountries. Experts also recommended collaboration in HTA training through the participation or hostingofinternationaltraining. Discussion AswithotherMiddleEastandNorthAfricancountries(MENA)(Fasseehetal.,2020),initiatives have been taken to implement HTA in Oman. Due to the strong political commitment, workshopsandwebinarsledbyexternalexpertswereconductedtointroduceHTAinOman (OmanObserver,2019,2021).TheseinitiativeshighlightedtheneedforanHTAroadmapto supportevidence-informeddecision-making.Consequently,aroadmapwasdevelopedbasedon experts'surveyandstakeholderrecommendations. Thesurveyresultscamefromascorecardthatwaspreviouslyusedinmanycountries (Csanadietal.,2019;Atikeleretal.,2023;Raisetal.,2020;Fasseehetal.,2022a;Almomani etal.,2021)tosupportHTAimplementation.Usingthesamescorecardallowscomparisons among different countries, which showed several commonalities in some key elements of HTAimplementationbutalsosomediversityinotheraspects. Withregardtocapacitybuilding,expertsinOmanrecommendedprovidingregularshort coursesandtrain-the-trainersprogramsintheshort-term(1-2years),whichwasconsistent withtherecommendationsofothercountrieslikeJordan(Almomanietal.,2021).However, Omani experts have placed a greater emphasis on increasing public awareness of HTA, reflecting a focus on transparency that aligns with Oman's Vision 2040. While many countries that applied the scorecard agreed to develop master's and doctorate degree programsinthelongterm(6-10years)(Almomanietal.,2021;Fasseehetal.,2022a),Omani experts expressed hesitation about developing such programs due to the country's small populationsize,whichmaynotsupportthesustainabilityoftheprograms.Consequently,the decisiontodeveloptheseprogramshasbeendeferredforatleast5years.
Intermsoffunding,OmaniexpertsexpressedapreferenceforadoptingasingleHTA Journal of systeminwhichthecriticalappraisalofhealthtechnologieswillbeconductedandfundedby Health the Ministry of Health, while assessments will be performed by the manufacturers. This Organization choice reflects the political will to implement HTA, which was reflected in the and recommendations of other countries that used the same scorecard like Ukraine (Csanadi Management etal.,2019).However,whatsetsOmanapart,isthatexpertshaveagreedthat,inthemidterm, theremaybeoutsourcingwiththirdpartiestoconductappraisalsduetouncertaintyabout 253 theavailabilityofsufficienthumanresources. Considering that most Middle Eastern countries have fragmented healthcare systems, (Fasseeh et al., 2020, 2022a; Almomani et al., 2021) most countries that used the same scorecard expressed apreference forthe presence of multipleHTA bodies.(Fasseeh etal., 2020,2022a;Almomanietal.,2021).Evenwhensurveyresultsindicatedapreferencefora central system, experts typically agreed during the feasibility and validation phase to establish multiple HTA bodies to avoid political conflicts that may arise (Fasseeh et al., 2022a;Almomanietal.,2021).However,inOman,decision-makersfromdifferentinstitutions agreedtoestablishacentralHTAbodyundertheumbrellaoftheMinistryofHealth,rather thanhavingmultipleagencies. RegardingthescopeofHTAimplementation,thedecisiontoinitiallyfocusoninnovative pharmaceuticalswithhighbudgetimpactwasconsistentwiththeresultsobservedinEgypt andJordan,(Fasseehetal.,2022a;Almomanietal.,2021)wherethescopeexpandstoalso includetherevisionofpreviousreimbursementdecisionsinthefuture. Forcost-effectivenessthreshold(CET),Omaniexpertsaimtoestablishavalidatedcost- effectiveness threshold within a timeframe of three to five years. Therefore, work must commencepromptlytoallowforthecompletionofapilotphaseandsubsequentadoption withinthespecifiedtimeframe. Omani experts decided to publish appraisal reports within 10 years, in addition to previouslypublishedappraisalrecommendationsandtimelines.Thedecisiontopostpone publishingcriticalappraisalreportstolong-term(6-10years)wasmadetoallowmoretime for improving their quality. In contrast, Egypt recommended to publish methodological guidelinesandtimelinesasamidtermplan(3-5years)(Fasseehetal.,2022a). Intermsoflocaldata,expertsindicatedthatthereisanexistingclaimsdatabaseinOman. This represents a strong starting point for acquiring reliable local data. However, some modificationstoitsstructurewillbenecessarytomeettheneedsofHTA.Oncemodified,the reliancewillbemainlyonlocaldata.Finally,regardinginternationalcollaboration,experts recommended participation in, or even hosting of, international training, as well as the exchangeofinformationthroughtheGulfCooperationCouncil(GCC). Nationalhealthcaresystems,includingOman's,donothavesufficientresourcestofund all new and old health technologies. Therefore, they must choose among different health technologies.Tochooseeffectively,HTAcompareshealthtechnologiesbasedontheircosts, clinicaleffectiveness,sideeffects,andotherfactors(Jooreetal.,2020).HTAthenprovides evidencetosupportandguidedecision-makersonthereimbursementofhealthtechnologies. Oman's2040visionhasestablishedambitioushealthcaresystemobjectives(Foodand AgricultureOrganizationoftheUnitedNations,2021).Suchobjectivesincludethecreationof a transparent system, providing high-quality services, and achieving universal health coverage(FoodandAgricultureOrganizationoftheUnitedNations,2021).However,with challenges facing healthcare systems, including expensive treatments, the rapid pace of innovation,theemergenceofgenetictherapies,andthegrowingnumberoforphandrugs,it isofgreatimportancethatOmantakesproactivemeasurestoensuretheefficientallocation ofresourcesandtheadoptionofnewcost-effectivehealthtechnologiesthroughHTA. AlthoughthereareseveralHTAimplementationframeworksinthescientificliterature describingHTArolesandimplementationplans,HTAroadmapscannotbefullytransferred
JHOM fromothercountriesduetovariousfactors,suchasthesizeofthecountry,GDPpercapita, 38,9 thehealthsystemstructure,legal,cultural,andpoliticalaspects(Kaloetal.,2016).Therefore, forOmantoimplementHTA,itneedstohaveitsownroadmapbasedonitshealthpolicy objectives. OurHTAroadmapoutlinesastrategywithspecifictimelinesfortheadoptionofHTA (Table 4). Moreover, creating a roadmap is only a step in HTA implementation. We recommend regular monitoring of actions to allow for the revision of timelines or 254 modification ofcertain action items. The HTAroadmap can also facilitateorganized and streamlinedimplementationofHTAenablingprogresstobemonitoredandfacilitatinga morerapidimplementationprocess. Limitations Our study had some limitations including the small sample size of survey respondents; however, we involved participants with rich knowledge about HTA and the number of survey participants was similar to studies which applied the same methodology in other countries. The low number of experts (sample size) implicated subgroup analysis by different employment statuses (public vs private), where the private sector was underrepresented in the study. Furthermore, patient representatives were not included duetotheunder-establishedpatientorganizationscurrentlyavailableinOman.Finally,we acknowledgethatthemajorityofoursamplehadtheirprimaryeducationinpharmaceutical sciences,withminimalrepresentationfromothersectors.ThisisbecauseexpertsinHTA andhealtheconomicsoftenemergefromsuchdisciplines. Conclusions ThephasicHTAimplementationplanforOmanidentifiesastrategicprogressionthrough immediateandlong-termgoalsovera10-yearperiod.Intheshortterm(1-2years),thefocus is on building capacity through training programs and integrating HTA education into healthcareprofessionalcurriculums.Additionally,earlyfinancingeffortsarecrucialforthe assessment (especially of pharmaceuticals with high budget impact) and the appraisal of healthinterventions. Formedium-termactions(3-5years),theplanemphasizesincreasingpublicawarenessof HTA, broadening assessments to include medical devices and surgical interventions alongside pharmaceuticals, expanding the HTA unit to accommodate a larger scope of technologies,anddevelopingaCETforOman.Overalongerspan(6-10years),thestrategy aimstofurtherwidentheHTAscopetocoveranextensiverangeofhealthcaretechnologies and ensure the publication of recommendations, critical appraisal reports, and clear timelines. This structured approach ensures a comprehensive integration of HTA into the healthcaresystem,enhancingdecision-makingatvariouslevels.Suchfoundationalsteps towardsHTAintegrationinOmanhavesetthestageforanevolvinghealthcaresystem that optimizes health outcomes and resource allocation through evidence-informed decisions. Movingforward,theactionplanmustundergorigorousevaluationtoidentifyareasof success and aspects requiring enhancement. This iterative process will ensure that HTA integrationnotonlyalignswithbutalsoanticipatesthedynamicneedsofOman'shealthcare landscape.Byfosteringanenvironmentthatencouragessystematicevaluation,Omancan achieveasustainable,evidence-basedhealthcareframeworkthateffectivelymeetstheneeds ofitspopulation.

About
Cookies are small text files that can be used by websites to make a user's experience more efficient.
The law states that we can store cookies on your device if they are strictly necessary for the operation of this site. For all other types of cookies we need your permission.
This site uses different types of cookies. Some cookies are placed by third party services that appear on our pages.
You can at any time change or withdraw your consent from the Cookie Declaration on our website.
Learn more about who we are, how you can contact us and how we process personal data in our Privacy Policy.
 Please state your consent ID and date when you contact us regarding your consent.
- [x] **Do not sell or share my personal information**

Guidelines for Health Technology Assessment Ministry of Health Sultanate of Oman
================================================================================
Guidelines for Health Technology Assessment Ministry of Health Sultanate of Oman
Author(s)
---------
**Said Al Rashdi, BSc, MSc**1, Asiya AL Kindi, BSc, MSc 2, IBRAHIM AL RASHDI, BSc, MSc 3, Adnan AL Qassabi, BSc, MSc 4, Manal Al Ansari, BSc, MSc 5, Safiya Al Muaini, BSc, MSc 1, Sara Al Balushi, BSc, MSc 1, Alia Al Suhaily, BSc, MSc 1, Ahmad Fasseeh, PhD 6, Zoltn Kal, PhD 7.
1 Directorate general of medical supply, Ministry of Health - Oman, Muscat, Oman, 2 Directorate general of medical supply, Minsitry Of Health Oman, Muscat, Oman, 3 Drug Safety Center, Ministry of Health - Oman, MUSCAT, Oman, 4 ROYAL HOSPITAL, Ministry of Health - Oman, Muscat, Oman, 5 Directorate general of medical supply, Ministry of Health of Oman, Muscat, Oman, 6 Syreon Middle East, Alexandria, Egypt, 7 Semmelweis University, Budapest, Hungary.
Presentation Documents
----------------------
*   [ISPOREurope25_Wani_ HTA167.pdf](https://www.ispor.org/docs/default-source/cti-meeting-21305-documents/dc9b1b1e-1c0b-44b9-9859-6df40f8f5d86.pdf?sfvrsn=79d8d654_0)
**OBJECTIVES:** Health Technology Assessment (HTA) plays a crucial role for optimal allocation of healthcare resources by providing decision-making, evidence-based information regarding healthcare technologies. Our intention was to create HTA methodological guidelines for Oman with the involvement of key stakeholders to facilitate consistency, transparency and robustness in appraisal process of health technologies.
**METHODS:** Guideline development included five steps: (1) learnings from international HTA guidelines; (2) multistakeholder workshop on key components of the Omani methodological guidelines; (3) survey to facilitate consensus on the most critical elements; (4) drafting of guidelines based on collected observations; and (5) validation through feedback from policy-makers and HTA experts.
**RESULTS:** The Omani HTA guidelines consists of six sections, including targeted indication, medical assessment, economic evaluation, budget impact analysis, social and ethical considerations, and transparency requirements. Evaluation of health benefits should primarily focus on policy-relevant outcomes, including mortality, morbidity, and quality of life, and utilizing the clinical assessment reports published by reputable HTA agencies is advocated. If the investigated health technology generates health gain to a policy relevant comparator, cost-utility analysis with quality-adjusted life years calculation, 3% discount rate for costs and outcomes and explicit cost-effectiveness thresholds is the preferred methods to judge the economic value of health technologies. The time horizon of budget impact analysis should cover a four-year period. Full disclosure of conflicts of interest, expert contributions, and a public version of HTA dossiers are mandatory to enhance transparency.
**CONCLUSIONS:** Acceptance of HTA methodological guidelines by the Ministry of Health represents an important milestone in improving the evidence base of policy decisions in Oman and provides a standardized and transparent approach to judge the value and affordability of health technologies, aligning with international best practices and local healthcare needs and priorities.
Conference/Value in Health Info
-------------------------------
 2025-11, ISPOR Europe 2025, Glasgow, Scotland
Value in Health, Volume 28, Issue S2
Code
----
HTA167
Topic
-----

Disease

A collaborative effort sets a national standard for evidence-based resource allocation in healthcare, aligning global best practices with Oman's local priorities. Saudi Arabia's universal health coverage score has reached 83, alongside a steady rise in life expectancy toward 80 years. These outcomes reflect more than incremental improvement. They point to a healthcare system that is becoming more integrated, more digital, and more outcome-driven under Vision 2030. Policy alignment, regulatory reform, and sustained investment are clearly translating into measurable gains. The next phase will be defined by how effectively innovation, access, and quality continue to scale together - turning progress into long-term resilience for the system and the population it serves. Regulatory approval is often treated as the finish line for market entry. In reality, it is only one milestone in a broader pathway toward adoption and scale. Visit our stall at [WHX Dubai](https://uk.linkedin.com/company/whx-dubai?trk=public_post-text) to engage with [Mohammed Abdul Kaleem](https://in.linkedin.com/in/kaleem-mohammed-?trk=public_post-text), Lead - Operations & Growth across South Asia, South East Asia, the Middle East, and Africa, to explore why regulatory success must be designed alongside procurement, financing, and service delivery pathways. In many GCC and African health systems, uptake is shaped by institutional purchasing cycles, reimbursement structures, and operational feasibility, not regulatory clearance alone. This systems-level perspective reflects how public and institutional health systems actually function. Strategies that account for policy priorities, budget impact, and service delivery realities are far more likely to translate innovation into sustained use and long-term impact. For life sciences companies, moving from market entry to market building requires regulatory thinking that is integrated, contextual, and aligned with health system goals. [![Image 33: View profile for Dr. Sara Al Dallal](http://www.linkedin.com/posts/syreon-middle-east_some-highlights-activity-7407405935364845568-c63e)](https://ae.linkedin.com/in/sara-ahmad-d?trk=public_post_feed-actor-image)[Dr. Sara Al Dallal](https://ae.linkedin.com/in/sara-ahmad-d?trk=public_post_feed-actor-name)  2w
    *   [Report this post](http://www.linkedin.com/uas/login?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Fposts%2Fsara-ahmad-d_the-rising-cost-of-healthcare-in-saudi-arabia-activity-7414514771020079104-Wwqs&trk=public_post_ellipsis-menu-semaphore-sign-in-redirect&guestReportContentType=POST&_f=guest-reporting)
 The Rising Cost of Healthcare in Saudi Arabia  Saudi Arabia's healthcare spending is steadily increasing-driven by population growth, ageing, and the rising burden of chronic diseases such as diabetes, obesity, and cardiovascular conditions. At the same time, Vision 2030 reforms are reshaping the system through privatisation, insurance expansion, and large investments in digital health, AI, and advanced medical technologies. While innovations like telemedicine and AI improve access and efficiency, they come with high upfront and operational costs. Workforce dependence, infrastructure expansion, pharmaceuticals, and system inefficiencies further add to financial pressure.  Key takeaway: Saudi Arabia's healthcare system is undergoing a necessary transformation-but sustainability will depend on: -Stronger prevention and population health strategies -Smarter, value-based adoption of technology -Better cost tracking and data-driven decision-making -Balanced public-private collaboration Managing costs is not about cutting care-it's about investing wisely to protect long-term health system resilience. [#HealthPolicy](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Fhealthpolicy&trk=public_post-text)[#SaudiArabia](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Fsaudiarabia&trk=public_post-text)[#Vision2030](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Fvision2030&trk=public_post-text)[#HealthEconomics](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Fhealtheconomics&trk=public_post-text)[#DigitalHealth](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Fdigitalhealth&trk=public_post-text)[#SustainableHealthcare](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Fsustainablehealthcare&trk=public_post-text)

Oman launches HTA guidelines for smarter health spending.
=========================================================
This title was summarized by AI from the post below.
[![Image 2: View profile for Pinal Patel](https://media.licdn.com/dms/image/v2/D5603AQHT0wUEo0LuGQ/profile-displayphoto-shrink_400_400/profile-displayphoto-shrink_400_400/0/1719677688231?e=2147483647&v=beta&t=p65U3URZFIYEbJ_2Z77q1cIDQAN81IL-TJivVU1Le2k)](https://in.linkedin.com/in/pinal-patel-adhrit?trk=public_post_feed-actor-image)
[Pinal Patel](https://in.linkedin.com/in/pinal-patel-adhrit?trk=public_post_feed-actor-name)
 9mo
*   [Report this post](http://www.linkedin.com/uas/login?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Fposts%2Fpinal-patel-adhrit_htaoman-oipcx2025-healthpolicy-activity-7316336738879131649-a14K&trk=public_post_ellipsis-menu-semaphore-sign-in-redirect&guestReportContentType=POST&_f=guest-reporting)
 Oman Just Activated the Engine of Smarter Health Spending. HTA Guidelines Are Here - And They're About to Reshape Everything. At OIPCX 2025, the [Ministry of Health Oman](https://om.linkedin.com/company/ministry-of-health-oman?trk=public_post-text) launched its first official Methodological Guidelines for Health Technology Assessment (HTA) - a powerful move that marks the start of evidence-based healthcare policymaking in the country.  What was implemented?  A national HTA framework tailored to Oman  Based on global gold standards from [ISPOR-The Professional Society for Health Economics and Outcomes Research](https://www.linkedin.com/company/ispororg?trk=public_post-text)&[EUnetHTA - European Network for Health Technology Assessment](https://nl.linkedin.com/in/eunethta?trk=public_post-text)  Localized through stakeholder collaboration  Built to guide how Oman chooses, purchases, and uses health technologies  Why does it matter? Because until now, decisions on new drugs, diagnostics, or medical devices were often made with limited data. With HTA, Oman is now able to:  Evaluate technologies based on cost, clinical benefit, and outcomes  Prioritize what actually works - and what delivers real value  Spend smarter, not just more  Align health investments with national goals under Vision 2040  How will it affect Oman's healthcare system? - Patients will benefit from access to proven, high-impact technologies - Hospitals and providers will gain clarity on what to adopt - The government will be empowered to allocate resources efficiently - Private sector innovators will have a roadmap for market access This isn't a policy change. This is healthcare transformation.  I'm Pinal Patel, CEO of Adhrit Consultancy. We work at the intersection of healthcare, technology, and policy - helping countries and companies navigate HTA, value-based care, and strategic growth. If you're in Oman or the GCC and asking:  "How do I align with this HTA vision?"  "How can my tech or solution be evaluated?"  "How will this reshape access and pricing?" Let's connect. Let's build smarter systems - together. [![Image 5: View profile for Dr. Sara Al Dallal](http://www.linkedin.com/posts/pinal-patel-adhrit_htaoman-oipcx2025-healthpolicy-activity-7316336738879131649-a14K)](https://ae.linkedin.com/in/sara-ahmad-d?trk=public_post_feed-actor-image)[Dr. Sara Al Dallal](https://ae.linkedin.com/in/sara-ahmad-d?trk=public_post_feed-actor-name)  3mo  Edited
    *   [Report this post](http://www.linkedin.com/uas/login?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Fposts%2Fsara-ahmad-d_hta-infrastructure-for-emirates-health-services-activity-7387012939754569728-qpqh&trk=public_post_ellipsis-menu-semaphore-sign-in-redirect&guestReportContentType=POST&_f=guest-reporting)
 Advancing Healthcare Value Through HTA: A Phased Framework for the UAE's Emirates Health Services The UAE takes a major step toward evidence-based and value-driven healthcare with the newly published paper "Health Technology Assessment Infrastructure for Emirates Health Services: A Phased Framework" by Dr. Suad Hannawi et al. (2025) in Frontiers in Health Services. This pioneering framework outlines a four-phase roadmap for institutionalizing Health Technology Assessment (HTA) within Emirates Health Services (EHS) - from early strategy alignment and budget impact modeling to full-scale integration of cost-effectiveness and patient-centered metrics.  Key Highlights: Establishes a structured, transparent approach to HTA across the UAE. Promotes value-based healthcare, innovation access, and financial sustainability. Strengthens stakeholder collaboration and data-driven decision-making. By embedding HTA into national health governance, the UAE continues to align with global best practices - ensuring that every healthcare innovation delivers measurable value for patients and the system alike.  New research in Management Research  The Journal of the Iberoamerican [Academy of Management](https://www.linkedin.com/company/aomconnect?trk=public_post-text) Systemic innovation in digital healthcare solutions: a framework for knowledge mobilisation by [Jose Miguel Natera](https://mx.linkedin.com/in/jmnatera?trk=public_post-text) and [Jos Luis Sampedro Hernndez](https://mx.linkedin.com/in/jos%C3%A9-luis-sampedro-hern%C3%A1ndez-13b48a2a1?trk=public_post-text) This article develops a framework to understand how digital healthcare solutions evolve by linking knowledge production, flow, demand, and application. Drawing on three case studies from Mexico, it highlights the importance of regulatory frameworks, contextual adaptation, and systemic innovation for effective digital health implementation. Canada's healthcare sector is entering a transformational growth era. Driven by population growth, demographic shifts, rising innovation in digital health, and sustained public-private investment, Canada's total healthcare spending is projected to grow at an average annual rate of 5.4% over the coming years. This surge means the sector is expected to exceed CAD $500 billion by 2030, up from CAD $372 billion in 2024, making healthcare one of the largest and most powerful economic engines in the country. This growth isn't just about scale, it reflects Canada's commitment to strengthening healthcare access, embracing technological transformation, and building capacity through a robust workforce strategy. From hospitals and infrastructure to digital health, AI and medtech, the sector's evolution is setting the stage for a more connected, resilient future. Source: Canadian Institute for Health Information & The Conference Board of Canada

Saudi Arabia & UAE: Leading the GCC Healthcare Investment Surge Between 2021 and April 2025, Saudi Arabia and the UAE accounted for nearly 92% of the GCC's 400 healthcare transactions, with the UAE leading at 198 deals and Saudi Arabia following with 170 Arab News. This surge reflects both nations' commitment to expanding healthcare infrastructure under national transformation programs, including [Saudi Vision 2030](https://sa.linkedin.com/company/saudi.vision.2030?trk=public_post-text) and the [Ministry of Health and Prevention - UAE](https://ae.linkedin.com/company/ministry-of-health---uae?trk=public_post-text) (2023-2026) strategy. The fastest-growing sectors? Digital health and AI. However, for healthcare providers, this momentum is meaningful only if it translates into improved clinician efficiency and enhanced patient care. At [HealthOrbit AI](https://uk.linkedin.com/company/health-orbit-ai?trk=public_post-text), we're focused on one lever with outsized impact: accurate, compliant clinical notes-automatically.     *   [Report this post](http://www.linkedin.com/uas/login?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Fposts%2Fppalav1972_healthcarestrategy-gcc-transformation-activity-7383764480599437313-aLsz&trk=public_post_ellipsis-menu-semaphore-sign-in-redirect&guestReportContentType=POST&_f=guest-reporting)
Why Healthcare Organizations in the GCC Are Transforming - and What Lies Ahead The GCC healthcare sector is transforming faster than ever - driven by competition, regulation, and the need for sustainable growth. In my latest post, I explore why transformation is no longer optional- and how consolidation, digitalization, and evolving regulations are shaping the next decade. [#HealthcareStrategy](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Fhealthcarestrategy&trk=public_post-text)[#GCC](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Fgcc&trk=public_post-text)[#Transformation](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Ftransformation&trk=public_post-text)[#Leadership](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Fleadership&trk=public_post-text) The GCC healthcare sector is at a pivotal moment. What began as a race to build world-class facilities has now evolved into a quest for sustainability, efficiency, and differentiation. 1) Rapid Vertical Growth: The region has witnessed a remarkable surge in healthcare infrastructure - from advanced tertiary hospitals to specialized centers and digital health platforms. This expansion, while impressive, has led to market saturation in several sub-segments, urging organizations to rethink their value propositions. 2) Rising Competition: Multiple hospitals, polyclinics, and niche specialty providers are now competing for the same patient base. In this environment,experience, trust, and outcomes have become the new differentiators - not just reputation or location. 3) Downward Pressure on Prices: With increasing capacity and insurance-driven negotiations, pricing power is eroding. Institutions are being forced to innovate operationally, optimize costs, and redefine service models to protect margins. 4) Post-COVID Acceleration: The pandemic acted as an inflection point - pushing digital transformation, patient empowerment, and remote care to the forefront. Healthcare delivery is now expected to be hybrid, personalized, and data-driven. 5) Evolving Regulations & Forthcoming Consolidation: As regulators across GCC countries strengthen quality frameworks, data governance, and licensing standards, a new wave of consolidation is likely to follow - where scale, integration, and efficiency will determine survival. The transformation we're witnessing is not merely structural - it's philosophical. The next decade will belong to healthcare organizations that treat transformation not as a response, but as a core discipline of leadership.

Evidence to Impact Series | HTA & HEOR Workshop We were privileged to have [Dr. Mahendra Kumar Rai](https://sg.linkedin.com/in/mahendrarai?trk=public_post-text), an esteemed expert in HEOR and RWE, deliver an insightful session on the topic : "Evolution of Health Technology Assessment in India and Global HTA Landscape." During the session, Dr. Rai elaborated on the evolution and process of HTA in India, emphasizing how it serves as a critical tool for evidence-informed policymaking and resource allocation. He discussed the proposal and reimbursement mechanisms associated with HTA and how they contribute to achieving equitable and cost-effective healthcare outcomes. Dr. Rai also provided a comprehensive overview of global HTA bodies, highlighting their structural and functional diversity across countries. He categorized them into matured, mid-level, and developing/budding HTA agencies, explaining their respective roles and contributions to healthcare decision-making worldwide. The session offered participants a deep understanding of the prospects of HTA in India, its integration into policy frameworks, and the significance of strengthening institutional capacity for evidence-based health systems. We extend our heartfelt gratitude to Dr. Mahendra Rai for sharing his expertise and valuable perspectives with our students as part of the "Evidence to Impact Series."  EDiHTA publishes its first scientific paper! We're proud to share our first peer-reviewed publication: "Shaping the Future of Digital Health Technology Assessment: Insights on Industry Challenges, Developer Needs, and a Harmonized, European HTA Framework." Published in the Journal of Market Access and Health Policy, the paper explores the perspectives of digital health developers and industry stakeholders across Europe on the current challenges and opportunities in Digital Health Technology Assessment.  Key insights include:  The need for greater transparency and harmonisation in HTA processes.  The importance of real-world evidence (RWE) and lifecycle-based approaches to reflect the fast pace of digital innovation.  The procedural and financial hurdles that SMEs face when navigating HTA and reimbursement systems.  Read the publication: [https://lnkd.in/eqaWYkYm](https://www.linkedin.com/redir/redirect?url=https%3A%2F%2Flnkd%2Ein%2FeqaWYkYm&urlhash=VJ1H&trk=public_post-text)[#DigitalHealth](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Fdigitalhealth&trk=public_post-text)[#HTA](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Fhta&trk=public_post-text)[#HealthInnovation](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Fhealthinnovation&trk=public_post-text)[#RWE](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Frwe&trk=public_post-text)[#EDiHTA](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Fedihta&trk=public_post-text)[#HealthTech](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Fhealthtech&trk=public_post-text)[Fruzsina Mezei](https://hu.linkedin.com/in/fruzsinamezei?trk=public_post-text)[Manos Tsiasiotis](https://it.linkedin.com/in/manos-tsiasiotis-57a5a21b1?trk=public_post-text)[Ilaria S.](https://it.linkedin.com/in/ilaria-sciomenta-092497281?trk=public_post-text)[Elena Maria Calosci](https://it.linkedin.com/in/elena-maria-calosci-a71308149?trk=public_post-text)[Debora Antonini](https://it.linkedin.com/in/debora-antonini-49a7b9152?trk=public_post-text)[Adam Lukacs](https://de.linkedin.com/in/adamlukacs?trk=public_post-text)[Rossella Di Bidino](https://it.linkedin.com/in/rosselladibidino?trk=public_post-text)[Americo Cicchetti](https://it.linkedin.com/in/americo-cicchetti-186a3628?trk=public_post-text)[Dario Sacchini](https://it.linkedin.com/in/dario-sacchini-47650417?trk=public_post-text)

 Implementation of DHTs in Europe is receiving growing attention - but what does industry think? We worked with developers across Europe to understand what helps or hinders DHT implementation in practice and how HTA could better keep pace with innovation. Our paper offers a deep dive into the needs and challenges of both small and large DHT developers, with a call for greater harmonisation, transparency and RWE-based approaches across Europe that may accelerate digital innovation   Read the publication: [https://lnkd.in/eqaWYkYm](https://www.linkedin.com/redir/redirect?url=https%3A%2F%2Flnkd%2Ein%2FeqaWYkYm&urlhash=VJ1H&trk=public_post-text)

 EDiHTA publishes its first scientific paper! We're proud to share our first peer-reviewed publication: "Shaping the Future of Digital Health Technology Assessment: Insights on Industry Challenges, Developer Needs, and a Harmonized, European HTA Framework." Published in the Journal of Market Access and Health Policy, the paper explores the perspectives of digital health developers and industry stakeholders across Europe on the current challenges and opportunities in Digital Health Technology Assessment.  Key insights include:  The need for greater transparency and harmonisation in HTA processes.  The importance of real-world evidence (RWE) and lifecycle-based approaches to reflect the fast pace of digital innovation.  The procedural and financial hurdles that SMEs face when navigating HTA and reimbursement systems.  Read the publication: [https://lnkd.in/eqaWYkYm](https://www.linkedin.com/redir/redirect?url=https%3A%2F%2Flnkd%2Ein%2FeqaWYkYm&urlhash=VJ1H&trk=public_post_reshare-text)[#DigitalHealth](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Fdigitalhealth&trk=public_post_reshare-text)[#HTA](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Fhta&trk=public_post_reshare-text)[#HealthInnovation](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Fhealthinnovation&trk=public_post_reshare-text)[#RWE](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Frwe&trk=public_post_reshare-text)[#EDiHTA](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Fedihta&trk=public_post_reshare-text)[#HealthTech](https://www.linkedin.com/signup/cold-join?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Ffeed%2Fhashtag%2Fhealthtech&trk=public_post_reshare-text)[Fruzsina Mezei](https://hu.linkedin.com/in/fruzsinamezei?trk=public_post_reshare-text)[Manos Tsiasiotis](https://it.linkedin.com/in/manos-tsiasiotis-57a5a21b1?trk=public_post_reshare-text)[Ilaria S.](https://it.linkedin.com/in/ilaria-sciomenta-092497281?trk=public_post_reshare-text)[Elena Maria Calosci](https://it.linkedin.com/in/elena-maria-calosci-a71308149?trk=public_post_reshare-text)[Debora Antonini](https://it.linkedin.com/in/debora-antonini-49a7b9152?trk=public_post_reshare-text)[Adam Lukacs](https://de.linkedin.com/in/adamlukacs?trk=public_post_reshare-text)[Rossella Di Bidino](https://it.linkedin.com/in/rosselladibidino?trk=public_post_reshare-text)[Americo Cicchetti](https://it.linkedin.com/in/americo-cicchetti-186a3628?trk=public_post_reshare-text)[Dario Sacchini](https://it.linkedin.com/in/dario-sacchini-47650417?trk=public_post_reshare-text)

[![Image 41: View profile for Dr Sneha Shankar, M.Sc.](http://www.linkedin.com/posts/pinal-patel-adhrit_htaoman-oipcx2025-healthpolicy-activity-7316336738879131649-a14K)](https://uk.linkedin.com/in/dr-sneha-shankar-m-sc-9b726a13a?trk=public_post_feed-actor-image)[Dr Sneha Shankar, M.Sc.](https://uk.linkedin.com/in/dr-sneha-shankar-m-sc-9b726a13a?trk=public_post_feed-actor-name)  3mo
    *   [Report this post](http://www.linkedin.com/uas/login?session_redirect=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.linkedin.com%2Fposts%2Fdr-sneha-shankar-m-sc-9b726a13a_i-attended-dr-elisabeth-brocks-webinar-activity-7386733435525951490-BRod&trk=public_post_ellipsis-menu-semaphore-sign-in-redirect&guestReportContentType=POST&_f=guest-reporting)
I attended [Dr. Elisabeth Brock](https://ch.linkedin.com/in/dr-elisabeth-brock-639b596?trk=public_post-text)'s webinar last week on the what makes Switzerland a compelling first launch market compared to other European countries such France, Germany or UK. It was thoroughly interesting and informative to hear facts about the Swiss Health system. For example, the health system ensures universal health coverage through "private not for profit insurers" in contrast to France and Germany with 95% patient satisfaction. Although there are high premiums, there is rapid access and high level of service. Some of the main takeaways for me regarding its launch potential were: -Pricing and reimbursement processes can run in parallel to the newly launched early access pathway allowing efficiency and early engagement. -The HTA Assessment is based on the WZW criteria: Wirksamkeit (Efficacy/Safety) Zweckmssigkeit (Usefulness/Appropriateness) Wirtschaftlichkeit (Economic Efficiency) - supported by a budget Impact Model with a full cost-effectiveness analysis is not mandatory. -Dossiers must be concise (<=30 pages), submitted in German, French, or Italian, with appendices permitted in English- It cannot be a copy paste from French/ German dossiers -Local expert input is critical to align with Swiss clinical and payer expectations. -Cultural and linguistic differences across regions should inform engagement strategies- Patient care is based on a combination of French, German and Italian practices with US guidelines being referred to commonly -Swiss KOLs are highly influential at global level and contribute significantly to international evidence generation and clinical practice standards: Engagement is key to -Important to keep an eye out on the Swiss landscape as it is constantly evolving.
